Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Rosales
Family: Moraceae
Genus: Ficus
Species: Fig
Nutritional components: Rich in protein, dietary fiber, various vitamins, minerals, and fatty acids, especially high in calcium, magnesium, and saturated fatty acids. According to measurements, every 100 grams of dried figs contain 3.6 grams of protein, 4.3 grams of fat, 2.9 grams of ash, 13.3 grams of total dietary fiber, 0.13 mg of thiamine, 0.07 mg of riboflavin, 0.79 mg of niacin, 5.2 mg of vitamin C, 363 mg of calcium, 67 mg of phosphorus, 898 mg of potassium, 10 mg of sodium, 96 mg of magnesium, 4.5 mg of iron, and 0.8 mg of zinc.

Name: Chaploo fruit
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Dicotyledons
Order: Rosales
Family: Rosaceae
Genus: Chaploo
Species: Chaploo
Nutritional components: Chaploo fruit has tender flesh and a sweet, fragrant taste. It is rich in protein, mineral elements, vitamins, and amino acids. Its calcium content is 24 times higher than that of apples, its iron content is 5 times higher than that of peaches (which are high in iron among fruits), and its phosphorus content is the highest among all reported fruit trees.

Name: Tree tomato
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Dicotyledons
Order: Solanales
Family: Solanaceae
Genus: Cyphomandra
Species: Tree tomato
Nutritional components: Tree tomatoes are rich in pectin, making them excellent for canning, jam, and pectin production. They can be eaten fresh as fruit, are rich in minerals and vitamin C, and have benefits for the spleen and stomach. When cooked, they are sweet and sour, with a refreshing flavor and rich nutrition.

Neem oil is used to treat rheumatism.

Name: Coptis
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Sapindales
family: Anacardiaceae
Genus: Coptis
species: Pistacia chinensis
Nutritional components: Pistacia chinensis is an excellent woody oilseed tree species, characterized by high oil yield and good oil quality. Research results have shown that the seed oil content is 42.26% (kernel oil content is 56.5%), seed oil yield is 20-30%, and the shell oil content is 3.28%. It is a non-drying oil with a light yellow-green color and a bitter taste, which can be used after refining. Fresh leaves contain 0.12% aromatic oil, which can be used as a health food additive and incense. The fatty acids mainly include palmitic acid, oleic acid, linoleic acid, palmitoleic acid, stearic acid, arachidonic acid, and linolenic acid. The combined content of oleic acid, linoleic acid, and palmitic acid accounts for about 95% of the total fatty acids.

Name: Moringa
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Brassicales
family: Moringaceae
genus: Moringa
species: Moringa
Nutritional components: Amino acids: Moringa contains about 20 amino acids, including several essential amino acids for humans. These amino acids are the basic units of protein and are crucial for maintaining human life activities.
Antioxidants: Moringa is rich in 46 antioxidants, which can scavenge free radicals in the body and protect cells from oxidative damage.
Vitamins and minerals: Moringa provides abundant vitamin A, B vitamins (B1, B2, B3, B6), vitamin C, and vitamin E, as well as minerals such as potassium, manganese, and chromium. These components are important for maintaining normal physiological functions, promoting metabolism, and enhancing immunity.
Protein and dietary fiber: Moringa provides high-quality protein and dietary fiber, which help maintain intestinal health, promote digestion, and enhance satiety.
Other components: Moringa also contains rich trace elements such as calcium and iron. Its calcium content is 4 times that of milk, and its iron content is 3 times that of spinach, which has a positive effect on preventing osteoporosis and anemia.

Order: Asterales
Family: Asteraceae
Genus: Artemisia
Species: Artemisia argyi
Nutritional composition: Contains volatile oils used as spices; also contains crude protein and cellulose for livestock feed, used as fodder in pastoral areas.

Order: Asterales

species: Artemisia macrocephala

Name: Flax
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
order: Geraniales
family: Linaceae (or Camelina family, but traditionally classified as Linaceae)
Genus: Linum
Species: Flax
Nutritional components: Seeds are rich in unsaturated fatty acids such as linolenic acid, an important oil crop; fibers can be used in textiles, with excellent moisture absorption and breathability; the whole plant and roots have medicinal value, such as calming the liver and extinguishing wind, tranquilizing and calming the mind.

species: Hemp

Name: Catechu
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Rosales
Family: Fabaceae
Genus: Acacia
Species: Acacia catechu
Nutritional components: The decoction of heartwood fragments, after concentration and drying, becomes catechu extract or catechu powder, which has functions such as clearing heat, promoting fluid production, resolving phlegm, stopping bleeding, healing sores, promoting tissue regeneration, and relieving pain. The tannin extracted from the heartwood is also an excellent raw material for leather tanning and dyeing in industry. The wood is hard and fine, suitable for use in sleepers, construction, agricultural tools, and carriages.

Name: Tea Maple
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Sapindales
Family: Aceraceae
Genus: Acer
species: Acer ginnala group
Nutritional components: The bark, leaves, and fruits of this subspecies contain tannins, which can be extracted to make tannin extract and also used as a black dye. The fibers in the bark can be used as raw materials for artificial cotton and papermaking. The dried young leaves can be used as a substitute for tea, which has the effect of lowering blood pressure. It is also a special beverage for silk workers in summer, as sweat falling on silk after consumption does not leave yellow spots. The seeds can be pressed for oil, which can be used to make soap.

Name: Antidesma montanum
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Malpighiales
Family: Euphorbiaceae
genus: Antidesma
species: Antidesma
Nutritional components: It grows in sparse forests at altitudes of 140-1500 meters. The leaves of Antidesma can be used to make a bath or drink, which is believed to ward off evil spirits and diseases, promoting health and well-being.

Name: Camellia ptilophylla
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
order: Gentianales
family: Rubiaceae
genus: Camellia
species: Camellia ptilophylla
Nutritional components: It grows under forests or in shrublands. On dry and poor gravel soil, the plants are dwarfed, and the leaves become thinner. Those growing by streams or in dense forests can reach 3-4 meters in height, with leaves up to 8 cm long. It is recorded that the bark of this genus has fever-reducing effects, but this remains to be proven.

Name: Apocynum venetum
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Gentianales
Family: Apocynaceae
genus: Apocynum
species: Apocynum venetum
Nutritional components: This species is a widely distributed wild fiber plant in China. The stem bark fibers are long, flexible, lustrous, and resistant to decay, wear, and tension, making them suitable for high-end clothing, fishing nets, leather threads, and high-quality paper. They are also used in national defense, aviation, maritime, tire cord fabric, machine transmission belts, rubber boats, and high-end raincoats. The leaves contain 4-5% gum, which is used as a raw material for tires. The young leaves can be steamed, fried, and rolled to make tea, which has cooling, anti-inflammatory, and heart-strengthening effects. The white, silky seed hairs can be used as filling material. The peeled stems can be used as insulating building materials. The roots contain alkaloids for medicinal use. The plant has many beautiful, fragrant flowers with a long blooming period and well-developed nectaries, making it a good source of nectar.

Name: Stephania tetrandra
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
order: Ranunculales
family: Menispermaceae
Genus: Gushanlong
Species: Gushanlong
Nutritional components: The roots and stems of this plant contain various alkaloids, such as berberine and palmatine, etc. It is commonly used as an antipyretic in Hainan folk medicine and also has good anti-inflammatory effects.

Name: Bai Liang Jin
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Primulales
Family: Myrsinaceae
Genus: Ardisia
Species: Ardisia
Nutritional components: The roots and leaves have the effects of clearing heat, soothing the throat, relaxing tendons, and promoting blood circulation. They are used to treat sore throat, tonsillitis, nephritis edema, rheumatism, and injuries. They are also used to treat turbid urine, bone tuberculosis, cough with blood from overwork, abscesses, and snake bites. The fruit is edible; the seeds can be pressed for oil.

Name: Bei Ma Dou Ling
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Aristolochiales
Family: Aristolochiaceae
Genus: Aristolochia
Species: Aristolochia
Nutritional components: This species is used medicinally. The stems and leaves are called Tian Xian Teng, which have the effects of promoting qi circulation, treating blood disorders, relieving pain, and diuresis. The fruit is called Ma Dou Ling, which has the effects of clearing heat, lowering qi, relieving cough, and calming asthma. The root is called Qing Mu Xiang, which is slightly toxic and has the effects of strengthening the stomach, regulating qi, relieving pain, and lowering blood pressure.

Name: Ying Zhao Hua
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
order: Ranunculales
Family: Annonaceae
Genus: Artabotrys
Species: Artabotrys
Nutritional components: It is a greening plant with extremely fragrant flowers, often cultivated in parks or near houses. The fresh flowers contain about 0.75-1.0% aromatic oil, which can be extracted to make Ying Zhao Hua concrete, used as a raw material for high-end perfumes, cosmetics, and soap fragrances, and also for scenting tea. The roots can be used medicinally to treat malaria.

Name: Artemisia anomala
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Asterales
Family: Asteraceae
Genus: Artemisia
Species: Artemisia
Nutritional Components: Contains volatile oils, mainly flavonoids, phenols, amino acids, etc. The whole plant is used medicinally. In southeastern provinces, it is known as 'Liu Ji Nu' or 'Nan Liu Ji Nu'. It has effects such as promoting blood circulation, regulating menstruation, clearing heat, detoxifying, reducing inflammation, relieving pain, and aiding digestion. It is used in folk medicine to treat intestinal, stomach, and gynecological diseases. In recent years, it has also been used to treat filariasis and can be brewed as a tea for its cooling and heat-clearing properties.

Name: Vietnamese Berchemia
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Rhamnales
Family: Rhamnaceae
Genus: Berchemia
Species: Vietnamese Berchemia
Nutritional Components: The roots, stems, or leaves can be used medicinally. They have effects such as dispelling wind, promoting diuresis, promoting blood circulation, relieving pain, and relieving cough and phlegm. They are mainly used to treat rheumatic joint pain, dysmenorrhea, postpartum abdominal pain, tuberculosis, acute and chronic bronchitis, jaundice, dysentery, traumatic injuries, fractures, and abscesses. Additionally, young leaves can be used as a tea substitute, and branches can be used to make nose rings for cattle.

Name: Taiwan Gouercha
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Rhamnales
Family: Rhamnaceae
Genus: Berchemia
Species: Taiwan Gouercha
Nutritional components: This species is distinguished by its smaller leaves with 6-8 lateral veins on each side; the sepals have a sharply narrowed short tip, differing from Kuling Gouercha. The roots are used medicinally for dispelling wind and dampness, dispersing blood stasis, reducing swelling, and relieving pain; farmers often use the branches to make nose rings for cattle; young leaves can be used as a tea substitute.

Genus: Berchemia
Species: Big Fruit Gouercha
Nutritional components: The leaf shape and drupe characteristics are the same as the original variety, but the leaves are hairless or only sparsely pubescent along the veins, or have tufts of hair in the vein axils, and the petioles are hairless, differing from the latter. The roots are used medicinally for dispelling wind and dampness, dispersing blood stasis, reducing swelling, and relieving pain; farmers often use the branches to make nose rings for cattle; young leaves can be used as a tea substitute.

Name: Duckfoot Tea
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Myrtales
Family: Melastomataceae
Genus: Begonia
Species: Duckfoot Tea
Nutritional Components: The whole plant is used medicinally. Boiling the leaves in water and washing the body can treat colds. Boiling the roots with pig brain can treat headaches or malaria, and boiling with pig kidney and consuming with wine can treat back pain.

Name: Black-faced God
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Malpighiales
Family: Euphorbiaceae
Genus: Breynia
Species: Breynia fruticosa
Nutritional Components: The branches, leaves, and bark contain tannins, with the bark containing 12.02%. The leaves contain phenols and triterpenes. The seeds contain fatty oils. The roots and leaves are used medicinally to treat gastroenteritis, sore throat, rheumatic bone pain, eczema, hyperlipidemia, etc. Boiling the whole plant in water and washing externally can treat boils and dermatitis.

Name: Calycopteris
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Myrtales
Family: Combretaceae
Genus: Calycopteris
Species: Calycopteris floribunda
Nutritional Components: The leaves are used as a tonic and detoxifying agent, consumed as a tea by women within 15 days after childbirth, and also used as wrapping leaves for tobacco. The fruit is used as a stimulant.

Name: Middle East Golden Camellia
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Middle East Golden Camellia
Nutritional Components: The seeds have a high oil content, and the tea leaves are widely enjoyed as a beverage. This species is similar to Camellia nitidissima Chi, but the leaves are shorter and smaller, elliptical, thin leathery, with inconspicuous serrations, which can be used to distinguish them.

Name: Sharp-calyx Tumor-fruit Tea
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Sharp-calyx Tumor-fruit Tea
Nutritional Components: This species differs from Camellia acutiperulata Chang in that the leaves are narrower, the flowers are shorter and smaller, the bracts are round, the sepals are leathery, and there are three styles. The seeds are hairy and have a high oil content.

Name: Camellia acuticalyx
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Camellia acuticalyx
Nutritional components: Found in evergreen forests at an altitude of 1,000 meters. This species has sharp bracts and sepals, a hairless ovary, and hairless seeds.

Name: Camellia albosericea
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Camellia albosericea
Nutritional components: Found in sparse mountain forests at an altitude of 1,550 meters. The leaves are relatively narrow, with fewer petals. The sepals and petals are covered with white silky hairs, and the ovary has 3 chambers. It has effects and benefits such as promoting appetite, refreshing the mind, and protecting the liver.

Name: Camellia arborescens
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Camellia arborescens
Nutritional components: Found in sparse mountain forests at altitudes of 1,000-2,000 meters. This species differs from Camellia sinensis O. Ktze. in having larger flowers, more petals, and longer pedicels. It differs from Camellia purpurea Chang et Chen in having hairless sepals, larger fruits, and thinner fruit skin. It has effects and benefits such as promoting appetite, refreshing the mind, and protecting the liver.

Name: Pu'er Tea
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Pu'er Tea
Nutritional Components: The main effects and functions of Pu'er tea include refreshing the mind, calming the nerves, improving eyesight, quenching thirst, and promoting saliva production. It also helps in lowering lipids, reducing blood pressure, and decreasing uric acid levels.

Name: Duo Mai Pu'er Tea
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Duo Mai Pu'er Tea
Nutritional Components: Harvested from the mountainous sparse forests of Mayi Village, Qimabaxiang, Luchun County, Yunnan, at an altitude of 1400 meters. Locally processed for drinking, known as Mayi Tea.

Name: Bitter Tea
Kingdom: Plantae
Phylum: Angiosperms
Class: Magnoliopsida
Order: Parietales
Family: Theaceae
Genus: Camellia
Species: Bitter Tea
Nutritional Components: Grown in mountainous sparse forests at an altitude of 1370 meters, with trees reaching 8 meters in height. The leaves can be up to 29 cm long and 9 cm wide. The tea has an extremely bitter taste and is consumed as bitter tea.

Name: Cicada
Kingdom: Animalia
Phylum: Arthropoda
Class: Insecta
Order: Hemiptera
Family: Cicadidae
Genus: Cryptotympana
Species: Cicada
Nutritional components: The nymphs of cicadas contain 68.83% protein, 9.15% fat, with unsaturated fatty acids accounting for 77.27% of the total fatty acids. They contain 17 amino acids and 9 mineral elements. Every 100 grams of nymphs contain 72 grams of protein, which is 6 times that of eggs (11.8%) and 4.3 times that of lean pork (16.7%).

Name: Ring-necked Pheasant
Kingdom: Animalia
Phylum: Chordata
Class: Aves
Order: Galliformes
Family: Phasianidae
Genus: Phasianus
Species: Ring-necked Pheasant
Nutritional components: The muscle of the ring-necked pheasant contains crude protein, crude fat, inosinic acid, cholesterol, amino acids, and fatty acids. The breast muscle of the pheasant contains 17 hydrolyzed amino acids, with the highest content being glutamic acid, aspartic acid, lysine, and leucine. The total amino acid content is 33.22% to 37.26%, with the ratio of essential amino acids to total amino acids around 0.40, and the ratio of essential amino acids to non-essential amino acids above 0.60. Additionally, 22 fatty acids were detected in the breast muscle of the pheasant, with the fatty acid content in the melanized green pheasant being superior to other pheasants.

Name: Alligator snapping turtle

Phylum: Chordata
class: Reptilia
Order: Testudines
Family: Chelydridae
Genus: Macrochelys
Species: Macrochelys temminckii

Name: Chinese sturgeon
Kingdom: Animalia
Phylum: Chordata
Class: Osteichthyes
Order: Acipenseriformes
Family: Acipenseridae
Genus: Acipenser
Species: Chinese sturgeon

It is also rich in highly unsaturated fatty acids, including DHA (docosahexaenoic acid) and EPA (eicosapentaenoic acid), known as 'brain gold', which are very beneficial for cardiovascular and cerebrovascular health, helping to soften blood vessels, promote brain development, and improve memory.

Name: Nile crocodile
Kingdom: Animalia
Phylum: Chordata
class: Reptilia
order: Crocodilia
family: Crocodylidae
genus: Crocodylus
species: Nile crocodile
Nutritional components: Crocodile meat is an excellent source of protein, with approximately 17.80 grams of protein per 100 grams of crocodile meat. It contains a variety of essential amino acids for the human body, including lysine, leucine, and methionine. The fatty acid composition in crocodile meat is balanced, containing monounsaturated fatty acids (MUFA) and polyunsaturated fatty acids (PUFA) that are beneficial for cardiovascular health, such as ω-3 and ω-6 fatty acids. Crocodile meat contains various vitamins (such as vitamin A, E, B12) and minerals (such as calcium, phosphorus, iron, zinc), with particularly rich levels of vitamin B12 and zinc, which help support the immune system and skin health. Crocodile meat also has a high collagen content.

Name: Chinese giant salamander
Kingdom: Animalia
Phylum: Chordata
Class: Amphibia
order: Caudata
family: Cryptobranchidae
genus: Andrias
species: Chinese giant salamander
Nutritional components: The muscles and skin of the Chinese giant salamander are rich in protein, accounting for more than 90% of its dry weight, and contain a variety of essential amino acids for the human body, making it a high-quality protein source. The amino acid profile in the salamander's muscles is complete, with 8 essential amino acids making up 44.40% of the total amino acids. The fat of the salamander has a high proportion of unsaturated fatty acids, especially polyunsaturated fatty acids such as docosahexaenoic acid (DHA), which are beneficial for cardiovascular health. The muscles and skin of the salamander contain various mineral elements, such as calcium, phosphorus, potassium, sodium, magnesium, zinc, iron, copper, manganese, and selenium, with selenium content meeting the standard for selenium enrichment, which positively enhances human immunity. The skin of the salamander contains a large amount of collagen and gelatin, which have positive effects on skin health and beauty. The salamander also contains functional components such as active peptides and polysaccharide peptides, which have effects such as regulating immunity, lowering blood pressure and lipids, improving corneal endothelium, and relieving fatigue.

Name: Asian Wild Elephant

Phylum: Chordata
class: Mammalia
Order: Proboscidea
Family: Elephantidae
Genus: Elephas
Species: Asian Elephant

The vitamins it contains are much richer than those in the meat of general warm-blooded animals.

Name: Rat Snake
Kingdom: Animalia
Phylum: Chordata
class: Reptilia
Order: Squamata
family: Colubridae
Genus: Rat Snake
Species: Rat Snake
Nutritional components: Rat snake meat contains various proteins and amino acids, making it a source of high-quality protein. It has a moderate fat content and contains unsaturated fatty acids beneficial to human health. It is rich in mineral elements such as calcium, phosphorus, and iron, which contribute to bone health and blood production.
